    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11028667375968906512">Tove Jansson's Moomin characters and books are admired the world over. In the United States the series beginning with <i>Finn Family Moomintroll </i>(first published in English in 1945) has accumulated generations of fans. Since Farrar, Straus and Giroux began reissuing the books in 1989, grateful readers old and new have been thrilled to have the stories available again. At last</span>
  <span id="freeText11028667375968906512" style="display:none">Tove Jansson's Moomin characters and books are admired the world over. In the United States the series beginning with <i>Finn Family Moomintroll </i>(first published in English in 1945) has accumulated generations of fans. Since Farrar, Straus and Giroux began reissuing the books in 1989, grateful readers old and new have been thrilled to have the stories available again. At last the final installment is being published – oddly, the only book that features none of the Moomin family themselves, though it does take place at their house. There familiar characters converge – Snufkin, the Hemulen, Fillyjonk, and others – seeking out the Moomins' welcoming company, only to find them absent. All remain at the house, all have very different personalities that clash often, but something about their homey cohabitation during the icy winter changes each visitor in a gratifying way. As <i>The Times Literary Supplement</i> put it, <i>Moominvalley in November</i> is "possibly the cleverest of the Moomin books."<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11028667375968906512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div id="review_4408941" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/4408941" />
    <a title="Zack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/172461-zack"><img alt="Zack" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/4408941?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zack" href="/user/show/172461-zack">Zack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9780510129958" href="/book/show/573671.Moominvalley_In_November">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4408941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9813188878874440560">Possibly the most melancholy children's book ever written. While the Moomin stories all have a slightly unnerving, mysterious quality, but this one is outright existential.<br/><br/>The idea is simple: What if there was a children's book where the main characters never showed up? Various supporting players from the other Moomin books converge on the Moomins' house, but they're just not there. Normally, this would lead to a quest story to find the family, but in his case, the Moomins are just away on a tri</span>
  <span id="freeText9813188878874440560" style="display:none">Possibly the most melancholy children's book ever written. While the Moomin stories all have a slightly unnerving, mysterious quality, but this one is outright existential.<br /><br />The idea is simple: What if there was a children's book where the main characters never showed up? Various supporting players from the other Moomin books converge on the Moomins' house, but they're just not there. Normally, this would lead to a quest story to find the family, but in his case, the Moomins are just away on a trip, and the other characters must learn to solve their problems without them.<br /><br />The tone of this is not unlike WAITING FOR GODOT or ROSENCRANTZ AND GUILDERSTREN ARE DEAD -- it's about the people who aren't part of the mian story, about an adventure that's not quite there. It's sort of a last hurrah for the Moomins, and it's a sweet story that fits its wintery mood. Life goes on in Moominvalley -- and life must go on for its fans as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9813188878874440560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Melki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293536-melki"><img alt="Melki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308071306p2/5293536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1443402884?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melki" href="/user/show/5293536-melki">Melki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780380007639" href="/book/show/10684676-moominvalley-in-november">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=kidstuff">kidstuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=keep-the-tissues-handy">keep-the-tissues-handy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1443402884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4778855739799214855"><b>What a weird little book!</b><br/><br/>This was my first visit to Moominvalley and apparently, I picked the wrong month . . . just like all of the characters in this book. They show up unannounced on the Moomin's doorstep, expecting solace and cheer, and instead they find emptiness and despair in a bleak, lonely house. The fact that the owners are gone doesn't stop the uninvited guests from making themselves at home, raiding the pantry and tracking mud into the house. And yet, life seems meaningless. They wan</span>
  <span id="freeText4778855739799214855" style="display:none"><b>What a weird little book!</b><br><br>This was my first visit to Moominvalley and apparently, I picked the wrong month . . . just like all of the characters in this book. They show up unannounced on the Moomin's doorstep, expecting solace and cheer, and instead they find emptiness and despair in a bleak, lonely house. The fact that the owners are gone doesn't stop the uninvited guests from making themselves at home, raiding the pantry and tracking mud into the house. And yet, life seems meaningless. They wander aimlessly through rooms while the relentless rain pounds outside. There is much hand-wringing and sighing.<br><br>This is the cover of my copy.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397096i/765960._SY540_.png" width="400" height="490" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Just look at them! Six miserable characters in search of a purpose.<br><br>In Greg's excellent review, <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64229241?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a>, he compares the book to a Bergman film, and he's right - this is terribly sad. There are no s'mores or campfire songs. No one suggests a game of <i>Monopoly</i>, and <i>Cards Against Humanity</i> hadn't been invented yet. In fact, if there was a love affair between elderly Grandpa-Grumble and the young, hot Mymble, this could be one of Woody Allen's later, unfunny films. <br><br>But all is not lost. The illustrations lovely and affecting.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447862288i/17059369._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="289" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447862333i/17059370._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="289" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And yet . . .<br><br>I realize that the Moomin books have been beloved by children and their parents for decades, but I'm having trouble picturing freshly bathed and pajama-clad tots sitting enthralled while Granny reads this passage:<br><br><i>In the long, vague dawn as the November night changed to morning, the fog moved in from the sea. It rolled up the hillsides and slid down into the valleys on the other side and filled every corner of them. <br>The fog had brought complete silence with it and the valley was quite motionless.</i> <br><br>Then she gave them castor oil, whipped them all soundly and sent them to bed.<br><br>Perhaps I'll visit Moominvalley again sometime. Maybe in May or July.<br><br>And I'll call first to make sure they're going to be home.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4778855739799214855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_64229241" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64229241" />
    <a title="Greg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42508-greg"><img alt="Greg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368721201p2/42508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64229241?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greg" href="/user/show/42508-greg">Greg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42508-greg?shelf=girls-girls-girls">girls-girls-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42508-greg?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42508-greg?shelf=books-for-kids">books-for-kids</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64229241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2989085025538368793">If you like your children books to be depressing and bleak you couldn't do much better than <i>Moominvalley in November</i>. <i>Edward Tulane</i>, might have had it's moments of despair, and had an overarching sadness to it, but next to this novel it's pretty fucking upbeat. <br/><br/>If Ingmar Bergman ever directed a children's movie it would probably be like this. Six depressed and solitary people separately decide to visit this one family that has always made them feel like life is worth living. Instead of finding t</span>
  <span id="freeText2989085025538368793" style="display:none">If you like your children books to be depressing and bleak you couldn't do much better than <i>Moominvalley in November</i>. <i>Edward Tulane</i>, might have had it's moments of despair, and had an overarching sadness to it, but next to this novel it's pretty fucking upbeat. <br /><br />If Ingmar Bergman ever directed a children's movie it would probably be like this. Six depressed and solitary people separately decide to visit this one family that has always made them feel like life is worth living. Instead of finding the family, they find an empty home and each other, none of whom really like any of the others. Then the six people wallow around the house and dwell on the futileness of their existence. I can almost picture Liv Ullman playing Fillyjonk and Bibi Andersson as Mymble. <br /><br />I am making this sound a little more bleak than it probably really is, but something about 2/3's of the way into this book inspired me to a not so good feeling depression. It takes something special in a depressing book to have that kind of impact on me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2989085025538368793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1432869198" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1432869198" />
    <a title="Hilary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42315986-hilary"><img alt="Hilary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445715101p2/42315986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1432869198?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hilary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hilary" href="/user/show/42315986-hilary">Hilary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those who have read the whole series </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42315986-hilary?shelf=houses-and-homes">houses-and-homes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42315986-hilary?shelf=great-illustrations">great-illustrations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42315986-hilary?shelf=losing-a-loved-one">losing-a-loved-one</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42315986-hilary?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42315986-hilary?shelf=female-author-or-illustrator">female-author-or-illustrator</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1432869198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8174850004358317727">3.5 stars<br/><br/>Having read and loved the rest of the moomin books several times over several decades, I was reluctant to read this final book written by Tove after the loss of her mother.<br/><br/>I don't think it's a spoiler to say the Moomin family do not appear in this book. Several friends come to their house and find them gone. A character called Toft, who is clearly based on the author herself feels this absence profoundly. Other characters miss the Moomin family and they tidy up the place and try to do s</span>
  <span id="freeText8174850004358317727" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />Having read and loved the rest of the moomin books several times over several decades, I was reluctant to read this final book written by Tove after the loss of her mother.<br /><br />I don't think it's a spoiler to say the Moomin family do not appear in this book. Several friends come to their house and find them gone. A character called Toft, who is clearly based on the author herself feels this absence profoundly. Other characters miss the Moomin family and they tidy up the place and try to do some nice things they think the Moomins will appreciate upon their return. <br /><br />The characters are all making an effort to try new things or be better versions of themselves, they try to identify the ruts they have become stuck in and do something to change. Grandpa Grump is the exception to this, he is far to stuck in his ways and ironically does not recognise himself in one part of the story.<br /><br />Towards the end of the book (mild spoiler) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the characters leave one by one, all except Toft who is left there alone  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The story was quite melancholy and although this was probably a fitting way to end the series, in which the characters were based on Tove's family and probably a cathartic one to write whilst morning the loss of her family, I didn't enjoy it anywhere near as much as the rest of the series. Although we are left with some hope (mild spoiler) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Toft thinks he sees a light, and wonders if this is the family's return <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It did feel very sad and slightly disturbing that the whole family had disappeared, rather than the Moomins mourning the loss of one of their family. After all Moomintroll is quite young still, a teenager I would guess.<br /><br />The illustrations are absolutely beautiful, there are many throughout the book. I'm glad my library copy was a hardback recent reprint which has Tove's original artwork on, unlike the other recent reprints that have insultingly got an illustrator to recreate an inferior version in pastel colours. Unfortunately the paper they used was quite thin so the print on one side shows through to the other, which is a dissapointing skimp on their part.<br /><br />I am glad I read this final book eventually but will probably not revisit and prefer to think of the Moomins continuing their lives happily in Moominvalley.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8174850004358317727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3444402921" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3444402921" />
    <a title="¸¸.•*¨*•♫♪SomeBunny Reads (Phoenix)•*¨*•♫♪" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84916113-somebunny-reads-phoenix"><img alt="¸¸.•*¨*•♫♪SomeBunny Reads (Phoenix)•*¨*•♫♪" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600928258p2/84916113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

Like everything Jansson writes, she reduces the plainest and most vital aspects of life to their component parts. Eloquent, mundane, and profound. It was delightful and it also broke my heart. <br/><br/>"How can there be so many sounds in an empty house, Fillyjonk thought. Then she remembered that the house was full of people. But somehow she still thought it was empty."</span>

<div id="review_51655987" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/51655987" />
    <a title="Oliver" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2193571-oliver"><img alt="Oliver" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392240834p2/2193571.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/51655987?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Oliver" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Oliver" href="/user/show/2193571-oliver">Oliver</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer51655987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16976285305724144667">In the previous book, the patriarch has a midlife crisis and moves the family out to a deserted island to allow himself to feel useful again. It doesn't work out too well, but the family manages to reach some level of peace and understanding of their surroundings by the end. Logically, they should return to their idyllic valley to prepare for winter. But when the six characters of the final book arrive at their house, all dissatisfied and searching for one thing or another, the family is still m</span>
  <span id="freeText16976285305724144667" style="display:none">In the previous book, the patriarch has a midlife crisis and moves the family out to a deserted island to allow himself to feel useful again. It doesn't work out too well, but the family manages to reach some level of peace and understanding of their surroundings by the end. Logically, they should return to their idyllic valley to prepare for winter. But when the six characters of the final book arrive at their house, all dissatisfied and searching for one thing or another, the family is still missing. Tove Jansson, in the saddest and strangest of her children's (?) books, tells her audience that they'll have to go on without her, and work out their problems as best they can. The warm and comforting Moominvalley is gone - Jansson couldn't reach it any more, and the series was becoming a burden. <br /><br />Much of the novel can be read as Jansson looking back at her creation with no small amount of regret - Toft serves as the young, innocent Tove, not realizing what she's going to unleash on the world with her imagination. "You want to be careful not to let things get too big," warns Snufkin, whose own worth gets called into question as he does his best to avoid the group of neurotics who are disturbing his search for a quiet place to write a song. Snufkin is the coolest character in town - in a letter to Jansson a reader requests a drawing to tattoo on his arm "as a symbol of freedom." But what use is he when someone needs help? No one feels comfortable enough to talk to the one who from outward appearances has it all figured out and doesn't want to be bothered. Throughout the book Jansson seems to be asking herself if she's made a mistake, given people the wrong idea, promised too much that she couldn't deliver. And yet by the end, the absence has served to allow our difficult, mildly irritating protagonists to learn a bit more about themselves, their abilities and limitations, and those of the family they once idolized or took for granted. Toft, the creator, stays to wait for the eventual return, but the rest walk away from the series, a little hardened but a little more complete.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16976285305724144667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_234976085" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/234976085" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5875398-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599578317p2/5875398.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/234976085?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/5875398-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5875398-rebecca?shelf=childrens-or-ya">childrens-or-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5875398-rebecca?shelf=lit-in-translation">lit-in-translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5875398-rebecca?shelf=scandinavian">scandinavian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer234976085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9802925999403710323">Here’s an offbeat selection for November. Strangely dark for a children’s book, it’s the last in the Moomins series. Tove Jansson said that after the Second World War she was depressed and wanted to write about something naïve and innocent. She wrote the first book of the Moomins series in 1945, about a family of hippo-like white trolls. The Moomins are well known and loved by many European children, but I suspect this book is more obscure and less lighthearted than the rest. Perhaps Jansson exp</span>
  <span id="freeText9802925999403710323" style="display:none">Here’s an offbeat selection for November. Strangely dark for a children’s book, it’s the last in the Moomins series. Tove Jansson said that after the Second World War she was depressed and wanted to write about something naïve and innocent. She wrote the first book of the Moomins series in 1945, about a family of hippo-like white trolls. The Moomins are well known and loved by many European children, but I suspect this book is more obscure and less lighthearted than the rest. Perhaps Jansson expects her child readers to have grown up with her enough to appreciate a more melancholy story.<br /><br />The Moomins do not in fact appear in this book at all. It is November, the days are closing in, and no one knows where the Moomins have gone and when they might come back. A series of visitors journey to Moominvalley and find the house empty, cold and strange; these interlopers try to make their own merriment with a picnic and a party, but it all falls flat. It seems the cozy, jolly world of the Moomins is gone. <br /><br />Our cast of six main creatures (they all have paws) are: Fillyjonk, made neurotic by a disastrous housecleaning experience; Grandpa-Grumble, a forgetful and irascible old gent; Mymble, a somewhat vain and silly creature; Toft, a waif longing for a (Moomin)mamma; Snufkin, who is trying to remember a five-note snatch of music he came up with last time he was in Moominvalley; and Hemulen, who has little confidence in himself but thinks he has to arrange things for everyone else.<br />	<br />Perhaps the most fun aspect of the book is Jansson’s original black and white line drawings of her peculiarly loveable creations. The book also felt unique to me for its Scandinavian qualities: the strange sprite-like creatures, woodland settings and short winter days, and the slight air of depression. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[One by one the creatures depart until only Toft is left. I worried the book would end with rather nihilistic pessimism – Toft staring out at a bleak sea – but in fact there is a glimmer of hope: Toft spies the Moomins’ boat approaching and runs to meet them. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />As with the best children’s fiction, there is much here to entertain adults. Some of the more sad and wistful passages seem particularly meant for older readers, though there is no reason why children cannot identify with them as well. Here is my favorite:<br /><blockquote>The quiet transition from autumn to winter is not a bad time at all. It’s a time for protecting and securing things and for making sure you’ve got in as many supplies as you can. It’s nice to gather together everything you possess as close to you as possible, to store up your warmth and your thoughts and burrow yourself into a deep hole inside, a core of safety where you can defend what is important and precious and your very own. Then the cold and the storms and the darkness can do their worst. They can grope their way up the walls looking for a way in, but they won’t find one, everything is shut, and you sit inside, laughing in your warmth and your solitude, for you have had foresight.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="9802925999403710323" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_802923824" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/802923824" />
    <a title="Petra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11861720-petra"><img alt="Petra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529581246p2/11861720.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/802923824?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petra" href="/user/show/11861720-petra">Petra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11861720-petra?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer802923824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16296875615122984829">Moominvalley in November is the last book in The Moomins series and definitely one of my favourite books written by Tove Jansson. It is terribly underrated but I think it is easily the best in the Moomin series. It is a lot darker, harsh and mature as the nature is in November. I do think that it doesn't work well as a book for both adults and children as the other Moomin books do but I thoroughly enjoy the novel every time I reread it and would recommend to pick this up even if you have never r</span>
  <span id="freeText16296875615122984829" style="display:none">Moominvalley in November is the last book in The Moomins series and definitely one of my favourite books written by Tove Jansson. It is terribly underrated but I think it is easily the best in the Moomin series. It is a lot darker, harsh and mature as the nature is in November. I do think that it doesn't work well as a book for both adults and children as the other Moomin books do but I thoroughly enjoy the novel every time I reread it and would recommend to pick this up even if you have never read anything by Tove Jansson. It follows a number of characters who all gather in the empty Moominvalley after the family has mysteriously left and abandoned the house. All of these characters have their own fears and thoughts that are intensified in the cold and lonely house. I do think that the absence of the center family, Moomins, creates a brilliant atmosphere and I love how lonely the whole book is. Like every Moomin book, it deals with heavy topics as fears, loneliness and death. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16296875615122984829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Amina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5079848-amina"><img alt="Amina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561930055p2/5079848.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

<div id="review_1432268058" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1432268058" />
    <a title="Stephen Curran" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11677504-stephen-curran"><img alt="Stephen Curran" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574349718p2/11677504.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1432268058?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen Curran" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen Curran" href="/user/show/11677504-stephen-curran">Stephen Curran</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/13501131-moominvalley-in-november">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1432268058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6745654738741064471">"The Hemulen woke up slowly and recognised himself and wished he had been someone he didn't know."<br/><br/>Nobody writes about sadness with as much clarity as Tove Jansson. This is the ninth Moomins book. Over the series, the tone has grown incrementally more melancholic. So it seems fitting that, for this final volume, the Moomin family do not appear. It ends with an absence.<br/><br/>This is not an adventure like Comet in Moominland or Moominsummer Madness. It's the story of a disperate group of characters findi</span>
  <span id="freeText6745654738741064471" style="display:none">"The Hemulen woke up slowly and recognised himself and wished he had been someone he didn't know."<br /><br />Nobody writes about sadness with as much clarity as Tove Jansson. This is the ninth Moomins book. Over the series, the tone has grown incrementally more melancholic. So it seems fitting that, for this final volume, the Moomin family do not appear. It ends with an absence.<br /><br />This is not an adventure like Comet in Moominland or Moominsummer Madness. It's the story of a disperate group of characters finding themselves in need of comfort and support and making their separate ways to Moominvalley. But readers of the previous story know something that Fillyjonk, Hemulen and Toft do not. The Moomins have packed up and gone.<br /><br />I don't yet know a great deal about the author (her biography is on my 'To Read' list) but I get the feeling that each of the characters in this book represents aspects of her own personality (annoyingly, I can't remember the name of this technique; if anyone is able enlighten me, I'd be grateful). It's a terribly unhappy book. Even the illustrations have become very small. But it's beautifully crafted, and magical, and moving too. The final scene, with Toft on the sea cliffs, is a hopeful one, and brought a lump to my throat. <br /><br />It's amazing to me that Tove Jansson was able to take this crew of comical characters with names like Snufkin and Grandpa-Grumble, and create something universal and profound. I am going to miss this series very much. They are, to my mind, masterpieces of twentieth century literature.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6745654738741064471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15861412945669911504">I love Tove Jansson's Moomin books and discovered at an exhibition of her work in Helsinki that she is an even better painter. <br/>This quote clicked with me to reshape the structure of my coming book 'Burn My Letters' (see <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bit.ly/burnmyletters'>http://bit.ly/burnmyletters</a>)<br/><br/>'There are those who stay at home and those who go away and it has always been so.   <span id="freeText15861412945669911504" style="display:none">I love Tove Jansson's Moomin books and discovered at an exhibition of her work in Helsinki that she is an even better painter. <br />This quote clicked with me to reshape the structure of my coming book 'Burn My Letters' (see <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bit.ly/burnmyletters">http://bit.ly/burnmyletters</a>)<br /><br />'There are those who stay at home and those who go away and it has always been so. Everyone can choose for himself, but he must choose while there is still time and never change his mind.'<br /><br />My only qualm with this book is that its sudden ending with little sense of resolution (where ARE the family? when will they come home?) breaks structural rules, but hey, Tone Jansson has such a strong following that she gets away with it. <br /><br />Beautiful sense of place, of characters well defined. Must read more.</span>

<div id="review_3153828407" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3153828407" />
    <a title="Juushika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/616321-juushika"><img alt="Juushika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541586729p2/616321.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3153828407?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juushika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juushika" href="/user/show/616321-juushika">Juushika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/616321-juushika?shelf=genre-childrens">genre-childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/616321-juushika?shelf=seasonal-autumn">seasonal-autumn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/616321-juushika?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/616321-juushika?shelf=status-borrowed">status-borrowed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3153828407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17886803687455787644">The last two books in this series are functionally a duo. The friends who were notably absent in <i>Moominpappa at Sea</i> now come to visit the abandoned Moomin home. This book is more satisfying, both because it benefits from its relation to the previous book and because it has a better balanced tone: the plot moves faster, the book is shorter, and so the subdued and melancholy atmosphere is balanced against the character arcs; it feels like the fantastic short story collection. But it's also a weird</span>
  <span id="freeText17886803687455787644" style="display:none">The last two books in this series are functionally a duo. The friends who were notably absent in <i>Moominpappa at Sea</i> now come to visit the abandoned Moomin home. This book is more satisfying, both because it benefits from its relation to the previous book and because it has a better balanced tone: the plot moves faster, the book is shorter, and so the subdued and melancholy atmosphere is balanced against the character arcs; it feels like the fantastic short story collection. But it's also a weird place to end the series, and I wish the last two books could have somehow been combined into a single volume or arc.<br /><br />Insofar as a review of the final book is a review of the series entire: The Moomin series was never quite what I wanted it to be. Often too silly, sometimes weirdly sad, there was always something in the way of my ability to fully enjoy the quirky, bumbling cast and the evocative/fantastic elements. I think that could have been remedied had I encountered the series as a child, when I would have been more receptive to the humor and more likely to latch on to the magic. But even if my adult reading experience was flawed, the cumulative effect is memorable, often <i>because of</i> things I've seen as flaws. The shifting tone, the kitchen sink approach to plot structure, all are distinctive; it's playful and childlike and kind, but has an adult's insight that I imagine ages remarkably well. I can see why these are beloved of so many, and wish I'd been a better audience, but it was still time well spent.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17886803687455787644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1162298656" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1162298656" />
    <a title="Deana Morris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23648359-deana-morris"><img alt="Deana Morris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434262046p2/23648359.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1162298656?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deana Morris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deana Morris" href="/user/show/23648359-deana-morris">Deana Morris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1162298656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11696341202034432228">If you suffer from insomnia may I prescribe a Moomin book; guaranteed to lull your over active mind into gentle slumber within a few chapters.<br/><br/>I frequently revisit these beautiful stories in the small hours, always comforted by the truths we rediscover through the characters' exploits.<br/><br/>The November book brings together secondary characters and excludes the Moomins altogether. But it's none the poorer for all that.<br/><br/>I've never been a big hemulin fan, but I grew to quite like him in this story. And oh</span>
  <span id="freeText11696341202034432228" style="display:none">If you suffer from insomnia may I prescribe a Moomin book; guaranteed to lull your over active mind into gentle slumber within a few chapters.<br /><br />I frequently revisit these beautiful stories in the small hours, always comforted by the truths we rediscover through the characters' exploits.<br /><br />The November book brings together secondary characters and excludes the Moomins altogether. But it's none the poorer for all that.<br /><br />I've never been a big hemulin fan, but I grew to quite like him in this story. And oh, the Toft, so adorable. The more he reads the more he doesn't understand but he keeps going, facing his fears, learning to accept all that he is.<br /><br />Some characters are their usual selves - Snufkin is his usual free spirited heroic self and the Fillyjonk is as neurotic as ever while the Mymbel is quite beautiful in her all-seeing openness.<br /><br />Everyone seems to learn something about themselves as they come together, waiting for the Moomins in their house, getting along as best they can without the uber Mother, Moominmamma, to make everything all right.<br /><br />I read moomin books 40 years ago and enjoyed them then, but they really are for grown ups - grown ups who need to sleep more!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11696341202034432228" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/563765297" />
    <a title="Natalie (CuriousReader)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6548813-natalie-curiousreader"><img alt="Natalie (CuriousReader)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476533404p2/6548813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/563765297?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie (CuriousReader)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie (CuriousReader)" href="/user/show/6548813-natalie-curiousreader">Natalie (CuriousReader)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789150104738" href="/book/show/13495491-sent-i-november">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer563765297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16239439173879610290">In this book, the regular main characters of the Moomin world - the moomin family, are not present. Instead we're introduced to other characters like Hemulen, Tofft, and Snuffkin. I did enjoy reading about them as they all ended up at the moomin family's empty house and following their passing of cold, rainy days in late autumn. However many of my favorite characters were missing (My, moominmamma), so it's not my favorite book in the collection. I think part of the genius of Tove Janssons charac</span>
  <span id="freeText16239439173879610290" style="display:none">In this book, the regular main characters of the Moomin world - the moomin family, are not present. Instead we're introduced to other characters like Hemulen, Tofft, and Snuffkin. I did enjoy reading about them as they all ended up at the moomin family's empty house and following their passing of cold, rainy days in late autumn. However many of my favorite characters were missing (My, moominmamma), so it's not my favorite book in the collection. I think part of the genius of Tove Janssons characters is that they are realistic and relatable, in some way or another, even being a part of this very different universe. They are full of contraductions, of dreams that will never be fullfilled, of little quirks and bits that make them unique. Yet they all had the same idea of going to the moomin family when the cold wind arrived. It's a charming book perfect for this time of year to enjoy with a hot cup of tea. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16239439173879610290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2933237065" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4786333093937341727">I really liked this one. I loved the premise of the main characters not being in the story and how everyone handled it. Tove Jansson is a genius. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3483347907" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3483347907" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5129776-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1331301021p2/5129776.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3483347907?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/5129776-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780241344538" href="/book/show/37119758-moominvalley-in-november">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5129776-chris?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5129776-chris?shelf=moomins">moomins</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3483347907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer682265566208158074">Set as autumn is on the turn towards winter in Moominvalley, this last of all the Moomin novels is, as expected, a bittersweet tale of friendship, absence, loss and hope. Six disparate individuals feel a yearning to visit the Moomins in their valley, but when they all get there they find the family gone and the house empty. How do they react when they realise that and how do they get on with each other while they wait for the Moomins' return?<br/><br/>I loved this for so many reasons -- the apparent whims</span>
  <span id="freeText682265566208158074" style="display:none">Set as autumn is on the turn towards winter in Moominvalley, this last of all the Moomin novels is, as expected, a bittersweet tale of friendship, absence, loss and hope. Six disparate individuals feel a yearning to visit the Moomins in their valley, but when they all get there they find the family gone and the house empty. How do they react when they realise that and how do they get on with each other while they wait for the Moomins' return?<br /><br />I loved this for so many reasons -- the apparent whimsy hiding psychological insights, the individual quests the characters found themselves on, the autumnal atmosphere beautifully recreated with hints of hibernation and the faint promise of spring, and of course for the delicate line drawings that delight the eye.<br /><br />While it's common knowledge that the author wrote this after losing her 88-year-old mother Signe, and that a deep sense of loss pervades the novel, most readers will be intrigued by the interaction between the six characters in search of a meaning for the empty home they visit, and of their reasons for undertaking their quests.<br /><br />We are introduced to each character in turn in the opening chapters: Snufkin, Toft, Fillyjonk, a Hemulen, Grandpa-Grumble, and Mymble, Snufkin's half-sister. They make their ways to the Moomin house for different reasons -- to recall a forgotten five bars of music, to learn how to sail, to find 'a Happy Family', to see the fishes in a brook, to visit an adopted sister, or simply because the mood takes one. These are the ulterior motives; but as the story develops and the visitors meet up and stay in the valley, one begins to question whether these are the real reasons.<br /><br />Of course they all have unspoken fears and obsessions and yearnings for being there, but they won't realise that at first because they have to get along with each other, eating together, not talking at cross purposes, devising entertainments for mutual amusement. And maybe, just maybe, they will come to find what they've each come looking for before they depart back to their homes.<br /><br />There are so many lingering images after reading this that it's hard to refrain from listing them all. There's the shadow play devised by the Fillyjonk with the silhouette of the Moomin family sailing (as they were in the preceding novel <em>Moominpappa at Sea</em>); Grandpa-Grumble searching for the hibernating Ancestor and losing the crucial note from the Moomins; the orphan Toft imagining a Creature born from electrical lightning, growing and creeping around the house, based on his confused reading about protozoic <em>nummulites</em>. The lenticular <em>nummulite</em> fossils when sectioned appear as spiral coils, a perfect symbol for Jansson's narrative and the characters' journeys to Moominvalley.<br /><br />Ultimately it is the young Toft who remains when the others have gone, aching for the maternal figure of Moominmamma, looking out for the returning boat carrying the Moomins and Little My back home, their passage signalled by the storm lantern on the mast, a light in the darkness.<br /><blockquote>Oh what is life? 'tis nothing but a dream,<br />A vast and enigmatic flowing stream...</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="682265566208158074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('b7nr6cYLR5WF4MBBbVKPenTToV6rZj+DPTWgwbVfkgE/hoHY/kWdgVTu653j7dN0YWdffCDJGB47CQFEuz4+sg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MiaVz9G+kg0G2mOyWlDZTlL90q8yW579zW0iIfq8xoliGf/+6fBIGdfUSG7U74VAR0ksjbn0uWDLUYOk9N1qOg==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/45230.Tove_Jansson">About Tove Jansson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/45230.Tove_Jansson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1419249529p3/45230.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/45230.Tove_Jansson">Tove Jansson
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,423
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer388501824981479718"><b>Tove Jansson</b> was born and died in Helsinki, Finland. As a Finnish citizen whose mother tongue was Swedish, she was part of the Swedish-speaking Finns minority. Thus, all her books were originally written in Swedish.<br/><br/>Although known first and foremost as an author, Tove Jansson considered her careers as author and painter to be of equal importance. <br/><br/>Tove Jansson wrote and illustrated her first <i>Moomin</i> </span>
  <span id="freeText388501824981479718" style="display:none"><b>Tove Jansson</b> was born and died in Helsinki, Finland. As a Finnish citizen whose mother tongue was Swedish, she was part of the Swedish-speaking Finns minority. Thus, all her books were originally written in Swedish.<br /><br />Although known first and foremost as an author, Tove Jansson considered her careers as author and painter to be of equal importance. <br /><br />Tove Jansson wrote and illustrated her first <i>Moomin</i> book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3300083-the-moomins-and-the-great-flood" rel="nofollow noopener">The Moomins and the Great Flood</a> (1945), during World War II. She said later that the war had depressed her, and she had wanted to write something naive and innocent. Besides the <i>Moomin</i> novels and short stories, Tove Jansson also wrote and illustrated four original and highly popular picture books.<br /><br />Jansson's <i>Moomin</i> books have been translated into 33 languages. </span>
  <a data-text-id="388501824981479718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Lie on the bridge and watch the water flowing past. Or run, or wade through the swamp in your red boots. Or roll yourself up and listen to the rain falling on the roof. It's very easy to enjoy yourself.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/460427-lie-on-the-bridge-and-watch-the-water-flowing-past">116 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;The quiet transition from autumn to winter is not a bad time at all. It's a time for protecting and securing things and for making sure you've got in as many supplies as you can. It's nice to gather together everything you possess as close to you as possible, to store up your warmth and your thoughts and burrow yourself into a deep hole inside, a core of safety where you can defend what is important and precious and your very own. Then the cold and the storms and the darkness can do their worst. They can grope their way up the walls looking for a way in, but they won't find one, everything is shut, and you sit inside, laughing in your warmth and your solitude, for you have had foresight.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
